  • D N A Replication in Escherichia coli is Initiated by Membrane Detachment of oriC An adequate model for the initiation of chromosome replication in Escherichia coli should explain why the introduction of multiple copies of the chromosomal origin of replication , oriC , does not perturb cells seriously and why such multiple origins are replicated synchronously ; it should explain why the key initiator protein , DnaA , is activated in vitro by binding specifically to acidic phospholipids and why the Dam methyltransferase is essential for the correct timing of initiation ; it should explain why phospholipid synthesis and fluidity are necessary for initiation .   • Results and Discussion Binding of DnaA and SeqA to the pR promoter region It was found previously that both DnaA and SeqA proteins bind to the replication region of bacteriophage l DNA .16,27 However , DnaA boxes necessary for DnaA-mediated activation of p bind R DnaA weakly , as they differ from the consensus DnaA box sequence in a few positions . [12742018]

[8449900]
  • When oligonucleotide templates were used in studies on SeqA -- DNA interactions , it was demonstrated that SeqA binds speciﬁcally to hemimethyl-ated GATC sequences , but not to fully methylated and unmethylated GATC regions .12,13 However , experiments with longer DNA fragments indicated that SeqA can also interact speciﬁcally with fully methylated oriC6 ,14,15 and other DNA regions .16,17 At the oriC region , SeqA binds speciﬁcally to two GATC sites , one on each side of the DnaA box R1 .14 It was proposed that this protein spreads to adjacent regions , which may result in competition between SeqA and DnaA for binding to DNA .14,15,18,19 Quite surprisingly , recent studies indicated that DnaA and SeqA , the main positive and negative replication regulators , are also speciﬁc transcription factors .16,17,20 -- 22 Both proteins can either activate or repress certain promoters , whereas activities of other promoters are not affected . [12742018]
  • This discrepancy may arise from the fact that , in contrast to the results presented here , interactions of DnaA with boxes of the consensus sequence , and of SeqA with a DNA region rich in GATC sequences ( the oriC region ) were investigated previously .14 Therefore , we decided to compar binding patterns of DnaA and SeqA on the basis of experiments with each protein added separately to DNA samples , rather than to analyse protein -- DNA interactions in the presence of both DnaA and SeqA in the same reaction mixture . [12742018]
  • Oligomerization via the N-terminus of DnaA is also required for the initiation reaction .6 Initiation of replication occurs once per cell cycle and , during rapid growth , at all origins in the cell simultaneously .7 DnaA binding to the low-affinity sites , as well as binding of architectural elements ( Fis , IHF , and HU ) , may possibly contribute to the synchrony of initiation .8 -- 10 Two main mechanisms prevent initiation from reoccurring at already replicated origins and involve either inactivation of the newly replicated origin ( by sequestration ) or inactivation of the DnaA protein ( by hydrolysis of ATP-DnaA to ADP-DnaA ) .11,12 Specific inactivation of new origins occurs because new origins are hemimethylated ( i.e. , adenine nucleotides of GATC sites are methylated on only one strand ) .13,14 The SeqA protein binds to the hemimethylated GATC sites and prevents remethylation by Dam methylase .15 Regions on the chromosome that have high numbers of GATC sites ( oriC and dnaA promoter ) remain hemimethylated considerably longer ( for up to one-third of a cell cycle ) than regions with few GATC sites .14,16 Also a region with an artificially high number of GATC sites ( an oriC-like distribution of GATC sites placed in the tnaA gene ) was found to be sequestered as long as oriC , showing that sequestration depends on the concentration and distribution of GATC sites .17 During sequestration of newly replicated origins , ATP-DnaA is hydrolyzed to ADP-DnaA in a process that requires the Hda protein and the DNA-loaded β-clamp subunit of the DNA polymerase III holoenzyme .18 This process contributes to lowering the initiation potential by lowering the proportion of ATP-form DnaA .19 The total amount of free DnaA is also lowered because new DnaA binding sites are generated by replication .20,21 After sequestration , the initiation potential is low , and initiation does not occur until a generation has passed . [18835566]
  • During most of the cell cycle , only the three highest-affinity 9mer DnaA boxes ( R1 , R2 , and R4 ) are bound by DnaA .22,23 The SeqA protein binds to newly replicated hemimethylated DNA24 -- 27 and forms large complexes that can be visualized by immunofluorescence microscopy .28,29 Each SeqA focus may contain several replication forks , although the exact composition of forks in SeqA foci may vary with growth conditions .29,30 SeqA complex building behind the forks may function to organize newly replicated DNA24 ,31,32 and may also have a role in chromosome segregation .33 In oriC , some of the low-affinity DnaA boxes ( I2 , I3 , and R5M ) also contain GATC sequences .34 SeqA prevents DnaA from binding to these boxes on hemimethylated oriC , but does not hinder binding to the three highest-affinity DnaA boxes during sequestration . [18835566]

  • Results from several independent investigations have shown the E. coli cell-cycle to be a composite of several autonomous cycles ( replication cycle , growth , and division cycle , etc. ) co-ordinated through signals and checkpoints .3 -- 8 The existence of a tight co-ordination between chromosome replication and cellular-growth is implied by : ( i ) the constancy of initiation mass over a wide range of growth rates ,9,10 ( ii ) mainten-ance of `` once and only once '' rule for initiation from oriC every generation11 ; ( iii ) synchrony of initiation from all the oriCs in every cell ( even for multicopy oriC plasmids ) during exponential growth ; 12,13 and ( iv ) the growth rate-dependent eclipse period .14 Three molecular mechanisms have so far been identiﬁed contributing to these co-ordination characteristics in E. coli : ( a ) transcriptional-control of the gene for the initiator protein , dnaA , through autoregulation ; 15 -- 20 ( b ) transition between the ATP and ADP forms of the initiator protein DnaA and titration of DnaA by the highafﬁnity chromosomal locus datA ; 21 -- 25 and ( c ) control of the re-methylation rate of oriC and dnaA gene by sequestration which leads to inhibition of the re-initiation from newly replicated oriC .25 -- 29 Inactivation of SeqA and perturbation of the meth-ylation rates result in asynchronous initiation along with a reduced eclipse period .14,30,31 The stable maintenance of the E. coli cell-cycle is clearly a result of the complex interplay among these functions and possibly several others yet to be discovered . [14643657]
